1933.03.13

The Enemy Outside the Pass Continues Fierce Assaults 1

Our Forces at Gubeikou Once Experienced a Change in Position, Regaining Their Original State After a Counterattack. Currently, Operations are Taking Place in Three Locations. Song Zheyuan Supervises the Troops at Xifengkou, Boosting Morale.

Division Commander Guan Linzheng and Brigade Commander Zhao Dengyu Wounded; Regiment Commander Wang Xuebo Killed in Action 2

(Beiping) This morning, Japanese troops continued their fierce assault on Gubeikou in the Sanjianfang area. The fighting was intense, and at 3 PM this afternoon, the battle had not yet ceased. Yesterday, our forces at Gubeikou indeed experienced a change in position, but after our counterattack that night, we regained our original state. Recently, fighting has occurred in three locations outside Lengkou: Lingyuan and D青山. A total of 156 wounded soldiers arrived in Beiping yesterday from the defense area and were sent to the affiliated hospital of the Army Medical School for treatment. (12th Dispatch)

(Beiping) A telephone call from Shixia Town reported that enemy armored vehicles charged our lines last night with fierce momentum, but were bravely repelled by our troops. The enemy suffered numerous casualties. One of our division commanders was wounded. (12th Special Dispatch)

(Beiping) After Song Zheyuan went to the front lines at Xifengkou to supervise the battle, morale greatly increased. Song strictly ordered that no guns be fired. When the enemy approached, our troops attacked with broadswords, killing over two thousand enemy soldiers. Our forces also suffered heavy losses due to artillery fire. (12th Special Dispatch)

(Beiping) There was no fierce fighting at Gubeikou today. Central Army Division Commander Guan Linzheng was wounded while directing operations at the front yesterday. He returned to Beiping today and entered Xiehe Hospital for treatment. (12th Special Dispatch)

(Beiping) Outside Gubeikou, our troops are defending various mountain ridges and passes, having built solid fortifications to prevent the enemy from advancing. The enemy repeatedly attacked our positions with large forces, but were repelled by our troops. This morning, the enemy again used more than ten aircraft to bomb our positions. At the same time, the enemy used light armored vehicles to cover their troops as they attacked the main force of our □□ Division. The fierce battle continued until noon today. (12th Special Dispatch)

(Beiping) A telephone call from Shixia Town reported that the enemy Hattori Brigade launched a fierce attack on our positions outside Gubeikou last night after 10 PM. Our □□□□□ Two Divisions and □□□ partially engaged in the battle. After an hour of intense fighting, the enemy failed and retreated to Sanjianfang. Our troops pursued, and both sides suffered heavy casualties. (12th Special Dispatch)

(Beiping) The fierce battle between the enemy Hattori Brigade and Song Zheyuan's troops at Xifengkou continues. Five enemy aircraft flew over Xifengkou again this morning to scout. Song sent a representative to Beiping this morning to meet with He Yingqin, reporting on the situation at the front and requesting that he quickly issue □□□□ to be transported to the front for use. (12th Special Dispatch)

(Beiping) Yesterday, the enemy used air force and heavy artillery to bombard our positions outside Gubeikou, and launched an assault with a large number of puppet troops. At 7 PM, our □ Division dispatched another brigade to attack from a small path. The enemy collapsed, with nearly a thousand Japanese and puppet troops killed. The enemy abandoned three armored vehicles, destroyed two tanks, and three field guns. Our Division Commander Guan Linzheng, a brigade commander, and three battalion commanders were all wounded. (12th Special Dispatch)

(Tianjin) A dispatch from the front reported that Song Zheyuan's troops resisted the enemy outside Xifengkou at 9 AM on the 11th. The enemy used heavy artillery fire to cover the infantry's advance. The fierce battle continued until noon, with four to five thousand enemy troops attacking the positions of the □□□ Division's Wang Brigade on the high ground west of Xifengkou. There were over ten hand-to-hand combats between the two sides. The fierce battle continued until the evening of the 11th, with both sides suffering hundreds of casualties. Both sides deployed reserves to join the battle, and the fighting continued as of the morning of the 12th. Song telegraphed that the enemy attacking our Xifengkou this time were the 13th and 14th Brigades. After three days of intense fighting, the enemy suffered heavy casualties. At 6 AM on the 11th, the enemy launched a fierce assault on us for three hours but was repelled by our troops. During the fierce battle, our Brigade Commander Zhao Dengyu led a special service battalion to supervise the battle. Brigade Commander Zhao was wounded, and Battalion Commander Wang Baoliang was killed in action. Brigade Commander Zhao, with the spirit of giving his all, led his troops out of Panjiakou despite his injuries, while Brigade Commander Tong led two regiments out of Dongjiakou. On the night of the 11th, they combined to attack the enemy's rear, capturing many enemy cannons, armored vehicles, tanks, and munitions, and burning the enemy's supply depot. (12th Special Dispatch)

(Beiping) This afternoon, Zhang Weifan, Chief of Staff of Song's troops at Xifengkou, reported by telephone that at 2 AM this morning, our Tong Zeguang Brigade attacked from Dongjiakou, while wounded Brigade Commander Zhao Dengyu still led his troops to assist from Panjiakou. Commander-in-Chief Song Zheyuan led the rest of his troops to advance from the front, making contact with the enemy's main force. The soldiers fought bravely, using broadswords and hand grenades in hand-to-hand combat. The enemy could not withstand the attack and retreated across the board. We are currently pursuing them, killing many enemy soldiers, capturing many spoils of war, and capturing over twenty enemy officers, who have been sent to a certain place in the rear and will be escorted to Beiping within the day. We also destroyed five enemy tanks and armored vehicles. (12th Special Dispatch)

Xifengkou: The Chinese troops retreating south of the Great Wall suddenly crossed the Great Wall into Rehe Province at 4 AM this morning, placing their first line at Fanjiakou. They attacked the mountain artillery unit of the Hattori Brigade, causing the Japanese commander, Nakahira, and others to fight with their swords. Due to being outnumbered, 15 were killed in action, and Commander Nakahira and 20 others were wounded. It is also reported that Commander Nakanishi and others have been killed in action. (12th Den-tsu News Agency Dispatch)

Guan Linzheng Suffered Five Wounds 3

(Beiping) Guan Linzheng suffered five wounds: one each to his right chest, left hand, and left thigh, and two to his right shin. All were caused by hand grenades. Guan said that he received orders to kill the enemy on the 26th of last month, arrived in Beijing that evening, and departed on the 28th. On the 4th, he gathered in Tongzhou and immediately went to the front line of Gubeikou to reinforce the right flank and engage the enemy. He led another regiment to occupy Long'er Town, covering the right side. The fighting was extremely fierce. By nightfall, several small areas had been retaken, and the enemy suffered many casualties. At dawn on the 11th, the enemy launched another attack on our right flank with over ten thousand troops, with 21 aircraft bombing fiercely and artillery firing like rain. Our troops fought to the death, suffering two-thirds casualties. By noon, they had advanced to our first line of defense. Our Regiment Commander Wang Xuebo was killed in action. Then, at a distance of only a dozen paces from the enemy, they engaged in hand-to-hand combat with hand grenades and bayonets. He encountered three bullets in succession and was wounded. Fortunately, the soldiers fought hard and were determined to sacrifice themselves. After a week of recovery, he will return to the front line. (12th Special Dispatch)

Sun Dianying's Troops Return to the Front Lines 4

(Beiping) The people of western Rehe are assisting Sun Dianying's army and have telegraphed the National Government, requesting that it send reinforcements to help Sun launch a counterattack. The rear echelon of Sun's troops has already arrived at the front line from Duolun. (12th Special Dispatch)

The Japanese Have Long Devised Schemes to Seize Rehe 5

(Tianjin) The number of refugees from Rehe arriving in Tianjin has reached two thousand. They did not stay but went to relatives and friends in various places. According to the refugees, a Japanese man named Pu Yi-san came to Linxi in 1920 with over twenty Koreans to open a hospital. In 1922, he established the Mongolia Industry Company in Dalian. His main task was to induce Mongolians to be pro-Japanese and to investigate the Chinese military and political situation. Mr. Pu was required to send a telegram to the Kwantung Army headquarters every day. After the incident, he went to Liaoning. After our army inspected the hospital, they discovered many detailed drafts of maps of Rehe. The Yamato Trading Company in Chifeng sold weapons to bandits to create disturbances. The people of Rehe and Mongolia were foolish and greedy for Japanese money, secretly leaking information. After the Motegi Cavalry Brigade occupied Kailu, it went straight to Chifeng in eastern Suiyuan. The tanks were the latest models, capable of traveling 30 kilometers per hour. Motegi spent heavily to buy over Liu Guitang in Linxi, Lindong, Tianshan, and other places, which was very helpful. Sun Dianying resisted the Japanese most fiercely, constantly selecting several hundred daredevils to carry out raids. Only about one-third survived each time, but they inflicted heavy damage on the enemy and obtained many new weapons. At present, counterfeit money has poured into Rehe Province with the enemy's iron hooves, and white flour is also being sold at low prices. Matsui has been planning to establish a Mongolian state in Dalian for over twenty years, spending tens of millions of dollars. Recently, he appointed Prince De of Mongolia as an envoy. The Baling Prince still opposes the Japanese invasion. The people of northern Rehe have launched a volunteer army led by Hu Baoshan, vowing to resist the Japanese to the death. (12th Special Dispatch)

Overseas Chinese National Salvation Army Commander-in-Chief Weng Zhaoyuan Takes Office 6

(Beiping) Weng Zhaoyuan wired, "Please, all newspapers, forward to fellow countrymen at home and abroad: It is noted that the Peiping Branch of the Military Affairs Commission of the National Government issued an appointment order on March 4, appointing Weng Zhaoyuan as Commander-in-Chief of the Overseas Chinese National Salvation Army. Upon receiving this order, I respectfully took office in Beiping on the 9th and immediately began training, to live up to the patriotic intentions of the overseas Chinese. I, Zhaoyuan, pledge my life to the country. Seeing the enemy's strength and feeling the people's anger, I will not hesitate to shed blood, even at the cost of my life. I hope that the strong men of the country will share the same hatred of the enemy, and that the heroes overseas will join in the plan to avenge our humiliation. If we work together, what enemy cannot be defeated? Moreover, the soldiers are the first to fight on the battlefield to eliminate the enemy, while the people are relied upon to encourage and support them. I hope that fellow countrymen at home and abroad will appreciate my sincerity and provide assistance so that the battlefields have sharp weapons and the soldiers have no fear of freezing or starvation. I respectfully telegraph this message and await your instructions. Respectfully, Weng Zhaoyuan, Commander-in-Chief of the Overseas Chinese National Salvation Army, bows." (12th Special Dispatch)

He Yingqin Arrives at the Military Branch to Take Office 7

Zhang Xueliang Flew to Shanghai from Peiping Yesterday Morning. Martial Law Headquarters Established in Peiping.

National Government Orders Appointments and Removals of He and Zhang 8

(Beiping) This morning at 10:30 AM, He Yingqin, along with Yang Jie and Jiang Bocheng, went to the Military Branch, summoned the staff and gave a lecture, hoping that everyone would work hard for the country with peace of mind. Zhang went to Shanghai for rest due to illness, and will return to Peiping after recovery. Wan Fulin answered on behalf of Zhang, saying that He and Zhang both worked for the country, and should obey in the same way. Also, Zhang has already left for Shanghai this morning. (12th Special Dispatch)

(Beiping) Zhang Xueliang flew to Shanghai at 9 AM this morning. (12th Special Dispatch)

(Nanjing) On the 12th, the National Government issued a clear order: Zhang Xueliang, Standing Committee Member of the Peiping Political Affairs Committee and Acting Chairman of the Peiping Branch of the Military Affairs Commission, requested to resign. He should be granted permission to be relieved of his duties. The order also appointed He Yingqin, Minister of Military Affairs, to concurrently act as Chairman of the Peiping Branch of the Military Affairs Commission. (12th Special Dispatch)

(Beiping) Peiping City established a Martial Law Headquarters, with Wang Shuchang as Martial Law Commander and Bao Yulin and Shao Wenkai as Deputy Commanders. Wang issued a notice today, strictly prohibiting rumors and incitement. (12th Special Dispatch)

(Beiping) Rong Zhen, Director of the Office of the Military Branch, resigned and will be replaced by Jiang Bocheng. Zhu Guangmu, Deputy Director of the Office, has left Peiping with Zhang and will be replaced by Chen Qinruo, Director of the First Division. Tang Guozhen, Deputy Director of the Third Division, resigned and has been replaced by Gao Shengyue. The Intelligence Division of the Political Affairs Committee has been abolished, and it has been decided to establish an intelligence agency within the Military Branch. (12th Special Dispatch)

(Beiping) Yu Feipeng arrived in Peiping this afternoon and went to the Juren Hall in Nanhai to meet with He Yingqin to discuss important matters. (12th Special Dispatch)

(Beiping) Jiang Bocheng said that the security of Peiping City has been entrusted to Wang Shuchang, Shao Wenkai, Bao Yulin, etc., to maintain as usual, and there is absolutely no need to worry. (12th Special Dispatch)

(Beiping) Yu Fengzhi went to Tianjin a few days ago and will soon go south to Shanghai. (12th Special Dispatch)

(Tianjin) The Japanese military in Tianjin declared to the outside world that if the Chinese army does not counterattack Rehe, it is believed that no accidents will occur in Peiping and Tianjin. (12th Special Dispatch)

(Beiping) The Political Affairs Committee held a meeting this afternoon. Wu Jiaxiang reported on Zhang's resignation. The committee continues to operate as usual. It is reported that the North China Party Affairs Office will be moved to Shijiazhuang. (12th Special Dispatch)

(Beiping) When Zhang Xueliang met with Chiang Kai-shek in Baoding, he stated that he was willing to go abroad. Chiang said that going abroad or living in Shanghai were both acceptable, and he would be needed in three to five months. Song also strongly urged Zhang to go to Shanghai and live with him. Zhang returned to Peiping and told his old subordinates. Some said that the situation in Shanghai was complicated and not suitable for going there. It would be best to find a place to live in a village in Baoding or Shijiazhuang. Zhang said that he had already agreed to Song and could not break his promise. Therefore, he did not leave yesterday morning. To avoid trouble, he instructed his department to notify various places, saying that he had left. In fact, Zhang still lived in the Shuncheng Prince's Mansion. He departed from the Shuncheng Prince's Mansion at 9 AM this morning. More than 40 people, including Rong Zhen, Wan Fulin, Zhang Zuoxiang, and Liu Zhe, saw him off. Zhang will stay in Shanghai for a few days and then buy a ship to live in Belgium or Italy. (12th Special Dispatch)

(Beiping) He Yingqin said that the Chairman of Hebei Province will not be changed. (12th Special Dispatch)

(Beiping) This morning, He Yingqin formally took office as the acting director of the Peiping Branch. There were rumors that the Military Branch would be abolished, but this has been verified as incorrect. Mr. He declared that he had no intention of replacing personnel and advised all current staff to continue working with peace of mind. Wang Shuchang, Commander of the Peiping-Tianjin Garrison, submitted his resignation but was persuaded to stay. Mr. He also denied that Yu Xuezhong had any intention of resigning. (12th Reuters Dispatch)

(Beiping) After Zhang Xueliang submitted his resignation to the Central Government, the Central Government, considering that Zhang's resignation was firm, and in order to allow him to have adequate time to recuperate, has telegraphed He Yingqin to act as Chairman of the Military Branch in the name of the Minister of Military Affairs. After receiving the telegram, Mr. He arrived at the meeting to work at 10 AM on the 12th. When reporters went to pay their respects at 1 PM in the afternoon, they were granted an audience. He said briefly that he had come north this time under orders to inspect. Now, because the Acting Chairman Zhang has resigned and left Peiping, the affairs here cannot be stopped for a day. Therefore, he has followed the telegram order of Chairman Chiang Kai-shek and is acting on behalf of everything in the name of the Minister of Military Affairs during the time that the Acting Chairman Zhang is away, so as to avoid interruption of duties. As for the organization and personnel of the Branch, they will all remain the same and will not be changed. All affairs will also proceed as usual. At this time of national crisis, when worries and anxieties are pressing, even though he has not recovered from his illness, he can only do his best to fulfill his responsibilities and work hard before Chairman Chiang Kai-shek comes north. It was also heard that after Minister He arrived at the Branch to work, he summoned all the staff for a lecture, encouraging them to work as usual for the party and the country. (12th Central News Agency Dispatch)

Japanese Consulate in Xiamen Sends Police to Arrest Residents Without Authorization 14

Without Prior Notification, One Policeman Was Shot Dead; The Xiamen Public Security Bureau Assisted in the Pursuit of the Murderer, But Was Unsuccessful

(Xiamen) Without notifying our official agencies to cooperate with our police, the Japanese Consulate sent three Japanese policemen on the evening of the 10th to arrest Chen Rongzhang, a Taiwanese resident accused of murder, on Minsheng Road in Xiamen. Chen opened fire to resist arrest. Japanese policeman Nogami Chikami was shot twice, both in vital areas. He first took a rickshaw, and at about 9 PM, the rickshaw was discovered by a guard on Zhongshan Road. He had already died on the rickshaw and was taken to the Third Precinct. The remaining two Japanese policemen, unable to pursue Chen, also came to the Third Precinct to recount what had happened. Lin Hongfei, Director of the Public Security Bureau, immediately arrived at the Third Precinct. The Japanese Consul also sent the Japanese Police Chief Kawawa Yanosuke to the precinct to request that a joint sea and land search for the murderer be conducted that night. Lin agreed to let the Japanese police cooperate with our police in the search. The Japanese Consulate sent an electric boat to cooperate with the marine police. Lin issued a special order allowing passage at sea for the joint sea and land search, which departed at 11 PM. At 12 AM, the Japanese Consul sent another person to cooperate with the Public Security Bureau to inspect the scene of the incident at the residence of Zhen Fumei at No. 11 Minsheng Road. Lin returned to the bureau at 12:30 AM. As of 12 PM on the 12th, the murderer had not been apprehended. The Public Security Bureau protested to the headquarters and the provincial government that the Japanese Consul had violated our sovereignty. (12th Special Dispatch)

(Xiamen) Another Japanese destroyer arrived on the 12th, making a total of three Japanese destroyers anchored in Xiamen. (12th Special Dispatch)

Originally, our Chinese nation is extremely peaceful, but because of various relationships in the environment and internationally, we must struggle ourselves. We must always remember these few words in the future and strive to practice them so that the doctrine can be clarified. Then, even though the Prime Minister has passed away, his spirit will last forever." (12th Central News Agency Dispatch)

Commentary

Japan's Intimidation Tactics 20

The Japanese army, under the guise of a puppet state, is invading Rehe, waging war while still wearing a mask of peace. Our country entrusted its defense to the wrong person, leading to the enemy's increased arrogance. Recently, enemy cavalry has even approached the Great Wall, with the alarming intention of infiltrating North China. Meanwhile, the Japanese military has issued an unofficial statement, the main points of which are:

"First, China must cease its anti-Japanese activities and, at an appropriate time, begin direct negotiations."

"Second, all anti-Japanese efforts must be stopped, or Japan will take self-defense actions."

"Third, the area within the Great Wall should be designated as a neutral zone, and the Japanese army will remain north of the Great Wall."

We have heard these kinds of arguments since the Mukden Incident and before the fall of Jinzhou. They are extremely insulting to us. At the same time, they use the familiar language of "special interests" and "acquired rights" common to imperialism to anesthetize their own people and manipulate other countries. They trample on our country's territorial sovereignty with iron hooves without any regard.

With the three northeastern provinces already lost and Rehe falling into enemy hands, even though we desire peace, the enemy continues to advance relentlessly. Now, they are repeating the old trick of Jinzhou last year, forcibly seizing our land and oppressing our people. The issue of "peace" or "war" has extended from the northeast corner to Hebei. They are forcefully demanding a neutral zone, even extending it south of the Great Wall. In reality, they are continuously sending reinforcements, planning to seize our crucial passes along the border, threatening everything from Gubeikou to Shanhaiguan. Their intentions are clear.

In today's world, although national borders are strict, the distance between countries has shortened due to convenient transportation. Japan's relentless aggression against our country, in terms of international relations, has become increasingly rigid towards other countries since the League of Nations accepted the report of the Nineteen-Member Committee. Justice and righteousness are on our side, but violent plundering is intensifying. Therefore, Japanese imperialism, after failing to coerce the League of Nations through intimidation, now intends to withdraw from the League. It not only disregards the League's covenants but also intends to extend its iron hand and crush everything with its cavalry. If the United States of America had not experienced an unprecedented financial panic and the European countries were not fully focused on their own security, our country might have been able to survive under a new balance of power among the nations. But now that the balance of power in East Asia has been broken, our country cannot even勉强苟安. Japan sees that its adventurous policy is beneficial, so it is becoming increasingly outspoken and unrestrained. In the past, it still hung up the banner of peace and pretended to advocate for arms reduction. Now, it is engaging in naked aggression, expanding its armaments. Its military budget of 820 million yen this year is already a wartime budget. The sudden outbreak of the Rehe war will likely increase it to over 1 billion. Moreover, soldiers in their first year (without completed training) account for more than one-third of the troops in the Sixth, Eighth, and Fourth Cavalry Brigades and the Fourteenth Infantry Brigades. Therefore, Japan's military expansion does not need to wait for the complete failure of the disarmament conference. Its intimidation of the world and its acts of aggression against our country are sufficient and more than enough to prove this.

So, why does Japan pretend to be peaceful, declare that it will not invade North China, maintain the Yangtze River, and promote Sino-Japanese friendship? Japan is known as a militaristic nation, with a war every ten years as its national policy. However, it relies on overseas sources for 90% of the raw materials and iron ore necessary for war. Its foundation is clearly unstable. It wants to absorb our country's iron ore and other raw materials, and the huge market in the Yangtze River basin is an excellent area for Japan to sell its goods. Therefore, the Japanese hope to maintain their existing business relationships in our country along the Yangtze River and coastal areas and strive to develop them, thereby reducing their domestic economic panic. At the same time, this can also help to adjust the military expenses for its invasion of the Northeast and Rehe. What could be a more skillful plan?

Therefore, after gaining Rehe, it uses the pretext of establishing a neutral zone to缓和our country's "national spirit" and stabilize the foundation of its aggression. After some time, the enemy cavalry may appear in the neutral zone again and窥平津骚扰河北. Our countrymen must quickly recognize the enemy's intentions, never lightly believe its sweet words, and never be afraid of its threats.

Verbal Sparring on the Sino-Japanese Question 21

Guo Taiqi and Matsuoka Broadcast Speeches in London

Lytton and Lloyd George Criticize British Policy

Japanese Privy Council Reviews Withdrawal from League of Nations Proposal

London Tonight, Japanese representative Matsuoka Yosuke and Chinese Minister to the UK Guo Taiqi will both use radio broadcasts to share their views on the Sino-Japanese conflict. Because the broadcast locations are different, the two did not meet. When Matsuoka arrived at the broadcast station, a group of communists took a hostile stance toward him, but the police prevented them from approaching. (Havas dispatch, 11th)

London Today, anyone with a radio listened to the broadcast speeches of Matsuoka, Japan's representative to Geneva, and Guo Taiqi, China's Minister to London. In his broadcast speech, Guo Taiqi strongly refuted the claim that Japan is a barrier to communism, stating that Japan's policy is to conquer the Asian continent, and that China is innocent. The Lytton Report and the League of Nations General Assembly have both stated this. Guo outlined China's progress since 1926, stating that China is not only not anti-foreign, but also prepared to cooperate internationally with Europe and America. As for Japan, it is a country of disruption, with anti-foreign sentiment permeating the entire country, especially in the last two years. For the sake of British and European interests, Japanese aggression must be stopped. If members of the League of Nations uphold the League's covenants, they can stop the aggression, and the aggression will stop itself. The Chinese people hope that Britain will set an example for the world by first refusing to provide the Japanese militarists with the materials they need for war. Britain only needs to make a moral claim, refusing diplomatic, financial, and commercial assistance to the aggressor, and it can eliminate today's war in the Far East and perhaps eliminate all future wars, he said. Matsuoka said that Manchuria is the cornerstone of the Far Eastern problem, so Japan cannot allow people who hate Japan to manage it. This is not only a matter of life and death for Japan, but also a matter of avoiding division and chaos in the Far East. Japan's inability to raise the Manchurian question in the League of Nations is like Britain's inability to raise the Shanghai case in 1927. Manchuria's development is due to Japan's initiation and its undertakings. The League of Nations did not seriously oppose Japanese troops assisting the Manchurian state in suppressing illegal elements in North and South Manchuria, so he does not understand why the League of Nations opposes Japan performing the same work in Rehe, because Rehe is part of Manchuria. Facts are gradually proving the soundness of Japan's actions in Manchuria. The Manchurian state is now on its way to achieving its wishes. Japan's only goal is to restore peace in East Asia and maintain it. (Reuters dispatch, 12th)

Tokyo Prime Minister Saito and Foreign Minister Uchida entered the palace yesterday afternoon at 4:00 PM to meet with the Emperor regarding the procedures for withdrawing from the League of Nations, requesting consultation with the Privy Council. After the preliminary review, the examination committee will be opened, which will take about two weeks to complete. It is expected to be submitted to the Privy Council's main conference for approval and passage, so the formal notice of withdrawal will be around the end of the month. (Electric Communication Dispatch)

The Danzig Problem: A Spark Ready to Ignite 42

The Polish Corridor: A Point of Contention Between Germany and Poland 43

Recently, Germany's attacks on the Polish Corridor Province have intensified. The so-called Corridor Province is the eight coastal districts between East Prussia and Germany. In 1919, it was unanimously decided by the Allied Powers after the European War to return it to Poland. Germany considers this an unfair handling of the Treaty of Versailles and vehemently opposes it. The truth of this matter is described below. After the establishment of the Treaty of Versailles, German ultranationalists strongly advocated making the acquisition of the Polish Corridor Province the core of their foreign policy, promoting it with all their might. The reasons for their dispute are nothing more than that the establishment of the Corridor Province is the most unfair measure against Germany, as the area formerly belonged to Germany and must eventually belong to Germany again. Secondly, the separation of East Prussia from Germany by the Corridor Province is unbearable. Thirdly, the majority of the residents in the Corridor Province are Germans. However, based on the facts: (A) Historically, the term "Pommern," which refers to today's Corridor Province, is a German term derived from the Polish word "Po-Morze." The names of the districts and rivers within the area are mostly similar. "Po-Morze" means "coastal area." German historians have stated that "Danzig" is a name derived from the ancient Polish word "Gdansk," which is a Slavic name and undoubtedly not of German origin. In the early 11th century, Polish King Bolesław unified the Polish territory, including all the areas known today as the "Corridor Province." In 1148, Pope Eugene III restored Danzig to the Polish diocese. In 1308, Teutonic Knights, at the invitation of the Polish King, came to preach in the remote area of Prussia. However, they betrayed their promise and occupied the land of the Corridor Province. In 1454, Poland finally recovered the lost territory. During the first partition of Poland in 1772, the Corridor Province was ceded to Prussia, while Danzig was annexed by Prussia during the second partition in 1793. Poland occupied the Corridor Province for about 700 years. It was not until the Treaty of Versailles in 1920 that the Corridor Province (excluding Danzig) was returned to its original owner, Poland, while Germany occupied the remaining provinces for nearly 148 years. (B) Ethnically, the majority of residents in each district of the Corridor Province are Polish people. Recently, the new German Chancellor Hitler stated that "the majority of residents in the Corridor Province are Germans," which is a mistake. During German rule, every representative participating in the parliament was Polish. In 1921, German residents accounted for only 19% of the province's population, and now it is even less than that. In 1927, German parliamentary speaker Laub declared, "We are fighting for the Corridor Province in our country (Germany), but everyone admits that the population of the province is Polish." (C) Economically, if we examine it from an economic perspective, the relationship between East Prussia and Germany has not been hindered at all. Since 1921, Poland has strived to adhere to a policy of transportation convenience. The German authorities are deeply satisfied with the speed and efficiency of the railway administration. Moreover, the Corridor Province is Poland's only access to the sea, and the lifeblood of the entire country is tied to this province.

Hitler's Speech After Election Victory Transforms Germany's Destiny Amidst Ten Thousand Cheering Listeners, Efforts to Eliminate Treaty Shackles 44

▲Berlin, 11th (Dispatch) Prussia will hold provincial and municipal elections on Sunday. Hitler also stated that the movement against Marxism is not out of hatred for laborers, but to save them from evil forces and prevent the complete collapse of the country. He stated that he does not harbor vengeful thoughts towards those who have hated us for fourteen years or foreign enemies. He is actually against war and is well aware of its horrors. Because he wants to achieve understanding, he is determined to restore Germany to a condition and position that makes it worthwhile for other countries to achieve understanding with us. National unity must be placed before international unity. He believes that this can be achieved. Interior Minister Frick, speaking in Frankfurt, stated that this revolution is not solely against Marxism. Any disturbances must be caused by foreigners impersonating members of the National Socialist Party to harm our movement. This has already been confirmed. Göring also spoke before demonstrators in Essen, stating that he intends to submit a proposal to the parliament to purify the officialdom, allowing corrupt officials to be dismissed at any time without receiving pensions. In special cases, they may be ordered to return improperly obtained funds. The process of purification has only just begun and cannot be completed immediately. Göring also mentioned the temporary closure of Jewish shops, stating that shouldn't the Germans tell the public not to shop at Jewish stores but at German stores? He believes that this is a matter of course. If he encounters anything that harms the Germans, he will use the police regardless of who is involved. However, he cannot protect Jewish shopkeepers with the police.

▲Hamburg, 11th (Dispatch) The Hamburg and Bremen East Asia Associations held their annual banquet here today, attended by over two hundred people. The audience applauded repeatedly. He stated that shortsighted politicians had attempted to shackle 60 million people for generations with the so-called Treaty of Versailles, not realizing that they could not treat a nation that had not completely lost its honor and self-respect in this way. Today, the German nation is happy to begin restoring its self-respect and abandoning the shame of the post-war era. We are forced to fight against treaties that are unnatural and unfair. Countries that are satisfied with the status quo often oppose attempts to change the status quo, so Germany's diplomatic position is quite difficult. It is often forced to make demands to maintain its unfair claims. At this time, some foreign countries still want to create a united anti-German front. It cannot be denied that peaceful methods are often difficult to change an unbalanced and unstable world. However, we have unwavering faith in the ability of the German nation to strive and achieve, which has given us the courage to undertake this arduous task. In short, there are only two paths in the world. If the Germans are not allowed to proceed along a fair and free path and become the guarantor of peace in the heart of Europe, then Europe will be close to an abyss.

Tang Emperor Xuanzong's Words During the Fengshan Ceremony at Mount Tai 46

丨Inscriptions on Jade Slips Excavated Beneath Mount Tai丨

Taian Correspondence: Jade artifacts and silk slips used by Tang Emperor Xuanzong during the Fengshan ceremony at Mount Tai were discovered at the site of the Haoli Mountain Pagoda beneath Mount Tai, as previously reported. It is now known that someone who participated in the excavation secretly rubbed a piece of the Fengshan Mount Tai text inscribed on the jade slip. The original text is entirely in the clerical script. It is transcribed below for those interested in the study of cultural relics. The text reads, "In the thirteenth year of Kaiyuan, in the year of Yichou, on the eleventh day of the eleventh month, Xinmao, the successor son, Minister Longji, dares to declare to the Emperor. The minister inherits and guards the great name, and is entrusted with this great destiny. He follows the earth's righteousness and serves as the extreme of humanity. He is respectful day and night and has not dared to be at ease. Relying on the blessings of Kunyuan, he has been granted auspicious omens, which have nourished all things and repeatedly ensured abundant harvests. He dares to make a tour of the times to repay the merits of the great earth, and dares to prepare jade, silk, sacrificial offerings, and all kinds of sacrifices for this burial ceremony to express his utmost sincerity. Emperor Ruizong Dashengzhen, who is paired with the gods as the master, may he enjoy."

Note: Kaiyuan was the reign title of Emperor Xuanzong of the Tang Dynasty, which was 1199 years before the founding of the Republic of China. Longji was Xuanzong's name. The above text seems to be a text for offering sacrifices to the Earth Emperor. It is suspected that there is also a text for offering sacrifices to the Heavenly Emperor. (March 10th)
