Free Talk

Patriotic Business 225

— Fan Zhongyun

Someone once compared us Chinese to Jews.

Jews are a commercially capable people, and I think the Chinese are even better than Jews at scheming and calculating.

Why? Let me tell you.

Jews are a people without a nation, while the Chinese nominally have a fragmented country.

Everyone says that the country should be loved. Therefore, even though the Jews have been without a country for two thousand years, they are still tirelessly working on the nation-building movement. Since our country has not been destroyed, the nation-building movement is of course unnecessary. What we have now is the patriotic movement.

There are many ways to love one's country: some resist, some resist in name but not in reality, some seek long-term resistance on their own, and some engage in "artistic salvation of the country" and "dancing salvation of the country"... In short, all of this is something that Jews cannot have.

What Jews cannot have is the strength of us Chinese.

Merchants say: big discounts are for saving the country. Amusement park owners say that dancing and movies are also for saving the country. Educators, of course, have even more sufficient reasons, saying "studying saves the country." As a result, business is booming, wealth is abundant, schools and shops are full of students, society presents a "calm" and stable appearance, and China is saved.

Soldiers brave in internal wars say: even one soldier or one soldier must fight to the end. However, once the military expenses are in hand, before the Japanese soldiers arrive, they will deduct the money and move to the concessions as landlords.

There are also those politicians who say: resist while negotiating. This is to use the slogan of resistance to do business with Japan. Rehe has already been given to Japan. Perhaps this deal has a possibility of being concluded?

From the news of Rehe's fall and the rise in public bonds, I saw the success of patriotic business.

The Chinese are truly worthy of being the second Jews - no, it should be said that the Jews are the second Chinese.

Empty City Strategy 226

— Lao She

The Japanese devils were startled,

Why is the city so quiet!

Could it be the empty city strategy, not even playing the zither,

Ambushes everywhere, heads falling one after another?

Looking from a height, they laughed,

It turned out that the old general was diligently practicing racing.

Large and small cars all head south,

Yellow sand rolling, wind mighty;

Thousands of boxes of luggage,

Tragic and stirring, private pockets full.

Who cares about losing the city and territory,

Anyway, no one can do anything to my old man!

Calculating abacus in Xiliu Camp,

Ten thousand, one hundred thousand, oh, where did that shot come from?

Central Army, is the enemy approaching the city?

Marshal! There are three dark figures jumping in the distance!

Ah! Waaaaaa!

Killing me, why didn't you report earlier?

The general, in a rage, withdrew from the city,

Running faster and angrier,

Running all the way to Turkey,

Living in peace and prosperity, and enjoying a long life.

The Japanese devils are also happy,

Everyone gets what they want, we are buddies.

Don't you see how the nation of Manchuria prospered?

Just dodge south.

Looking at the Positive Side from the Opposite Angle 227

— Zi Zhan

Because of a serious illness, I escaped from the hands of death, and my frightened soul was just calmed. My mind became clearer, and I lay quietly for a few days, thinking more. Unexpectedly, the more I thought, the more I understood. After reading books for twenty years, I didn't understand, but suddenly I had a flash of inspiration and suddenly understood everything. Ah, I just realized that positive articles should be read from the opposite perspective. For example, when you first arrive in Shanghai, you will always feel the lack of public toilets, especially in the French Concession. If you are a first-class idiot and sincerely believe the announcement "It is forbidden to urinate; violators will be arrested," even if you see urine flowing everywhere and the stench is overwhelming, you can only hold your bladder. Another example is that in the first-class carriages of trams, there are often Chinese and foreign notices saying "No Smoking," but I see many blue-eyed, high-nosed foreigners with cigars in their mouths, smoke everywhere, making people feel suffocated and headache. Not to mention that many advertisements in newspapers are deceptive, but even current event reports must be read with my "opposite perspective of positive articles" at least 70-80% of the time, so you won't be fooled. For example, if a place is cleared and the bandit suppression has come to an end, then the so-called clearing of a certain place is just driving the bandits from location A to location B. Clearing? He Long has died more than once, and there is still a He Long. Zhu and Mao have retreated from their old nest more than once, and they still occupy more than one old nest. As for everyone shouting "aviation saves the country," in fact, I have not seen a plane dare to return a bomb to Japan. Bombing bandits and sinking one's own warships is true. "Long-term resistance" is equal to long-term non-resistance, and "recovering lost land" is equal to "not recovering lost land." You have to look at their opposite meanings. In short, when we read books, do things, and live our lives, we must not be too serious about one side. In addition to positive articles, we must know that there is a reverse side. If you are too serious about one side, you will be known as unintelligent, or you will have the disaster of being beheaded. Things like overthrowing imperialism, overthrowing warlords, and overthrowing corrupt officials and evil gentry, many young people believe too much in these kinds of declarations and slogans and think of themselves as revolutionaries. Their precious lives are lightly given away, and they are even labeled as counter-revolutionaries. Some smart people just use these things as a cover. For small things, they have something to do and don't lose food and clothing; for big things, they are promoted and become rich and honored. Who cares about revolution or non-revolution? They just can't avoid writing positive articles on the surface. People who don't understand the "opposite perspective of positive articles" don't understand books, don't do well as officials, can't get rich, and aren't smart in life. One method is understood, and all methods are understood. I would like to contribute this unique secret to everyone. I invented it myself and do not have a patent.

Parisian Trifles 228

— Xiao Shijun, sent from Paris

When Lie Wen traveled to Europe, he wrote "Parisian Tales" and published them in Shen Bao, which was very popular among readers. Now Lie Wen has returned to China and is the editor of "Free Talk." He sent a letter soliciting manuscripts, so I wrote "Parisian Trifles" in response. I do not care about being considered a slavish imitator.

(1) Coffee Shops and Cemeteries

We usually feel that understanding a friend is not an easy thing. Some people say that to understand a person, you must first have feelings for that person. If you are indifferent to that person, or if you look down on them, even if you spend a hundred years with that person, you will never understand them. I personally agree with this view very much. I think that this should be the case not only for friends, but also for another nation and another country. Probably because I have lived in France for quite some time, I love it more and more every day, especially this novel and antique Paris. The reason I love France is because the French national character is somewhat similar to ours, especially in her humaneness. Yang Yun said, "What human emotions cannot stop, the sages should not prohibit." Su Laoquan said, "Those who are inhuman are rarely not great villains." In recent years, many people have criticized Confucius for his easy and humane words. Foreigners also compliment us when they say that we are humane and know etiquette and do not go against the doctrine of the mean. If it is said that our nation has strengths, I personally strongly believe that the strengths of our ancestors all lie in thoroughly understanding human emotions. This, of course, refers to the golden age of our intellectual circles during the Spring and Autumn and Warring States periods. After that, because the political system was autocratic, the intellectual world was also dark and gloomy, and no ray of light could be seen. But we can hear and see the grand scene that we now imagine based on books in the coffee shops and cemeteries of Paris. This is not a joke. All foreigners who have traveled to Paris generally have the same understanding. At a glance, there are more coffee shops in Paris than tea houses in our towns. Needless to say, most of the people sitting inside are talking. But sometimes they talk very profoundly. Many new philosophies and new literature started in coffee shops. For example, a coffee shop in front of the Panthéon was a place where the poet Verlaine visited every day. A certain coffee shop in Montparnasse was the place where the painter Manet and others gathered. The still-extant Belgian playwright Maeterlinck also met the pioneer of symbolism, Villiers, in a coffee shop when he was young and traveling in Paris. They got along very well and sometimes talked in coffee shops until dawn. If we want to investigate anecdotes of great figures, coffee shops are a treasure trove of such anecdotes. There is another reason why I value coffee shops in Paris, which is that you can see the character of the French nation there. As I have already said, what I love most is her humaneness. For example, if a few people walk into a coffee shop, if they talk about politics, whether it is the left wing, the right wing, the Communist Party, or even the royalists, if they talk about painting, whether it is impressionism, new impressionism, post-impressionism, fauvism, cubism, futurism, new romanticism, new mysticism, symbolism, neo-classicism, Dadaism, expressionism, or surrealism, they can all sit at a table and debate. Sometimes they naturally inevitably quarrel, but they will never quarrel to the point of being out of control. At most, they will ask the police to suppress it and then disperse. After dispersing, they still respect each other. They firmly believe in their own views and also respect the views of others. Therefore, Paris has extreme conservatives and also extreme reformers. This phenomenon seems very contradictory to people with narrow minds. But in the eyes of well-educated French people, it is not contradictory at all. They have a basic belief that people are not perfect and each has their own strengths and weaknesses. They do not believe that there are any flawless saints in the world, nor do they believe that there are any heinous villains. To give another example, in the four magnificent cemeteries in Paris, we see many great figures with very different schools of thought buried in one place. Although each person's thoughts were very different during their lifetime, they became close neighbors after death. This also shows the comedies and tragedies of life. There are four major cemeteries in Paris, each occupying one of the four directions: east, west, south, and north. Molière, La Fontaine, Béranger, Musset, Balzac, the painter Corot, Delacroix, the musician Chopin, and the historian Michelet are buried in the Eastern Cemetery (Pere-Lachaise). The father of modern music, Claude Debussy, and the father of modern painting, Manet, are buried in the Western Cemetery (Passy). In the Southern Cemetery (Montparnasse), there is a memorial statue of Baudelaire and inscriptions of Sainte-Beuve, Coppée, etc. Zola, Alexandre Dumas Jr., Renan, and the painter Millet have tomb steles in the Northern Cemetery (Montmartre). The red-faced and ill-fated Camille, whom the Chinese are familiar with, is said to be a real person, and we can also find her burial marker in this cemetery. In short, the French are not only good at sending life, but also good at sending death. The four major cemeteries in Paris are decorated very elegantly. Walking from the coffee shop to the cemetery, one cannot help but compliment them on their death and life being well placed.

The Black Woman's Prayer (26) 229

— By George Bernard Shaw, translated by Yi Xian

"Since value is a matter of comparison, how would she know your value unless she knew fifty or so men to compare you with?" said the black girl.

"Oh, God who made men and women like this! Please bless me," the Arab exclaimed in despair. "What am I saying? Oh, wouldn't a child with fifty fathers have no father?"

"What does it matter as long as she has a mother?" said the black girl. "Besides, what you're saying isn't right either. One of the fifty is her father."

"You must know," said the Arab, "that there are many shameless women who have known countless men; but they have not given birth to children; as for me, who pursues and possesses every woman I see who is pleasing to my eyes, I have many, many children. From this it is clear that this kind of unfairness to women is one of God's divine necessities, and it is useless to resist God. God is great and glorious; only He has majesty and power; but His fairness has not been understood by us. My pampered wives suffer so much when they give birth to children, and every time I hear their cries, my heart cannot help but tighten; such pain is something we men cannot endure. This is not fair; if the only way to remedy such unfairness is to let women do men's things and men do women's things, do you think I can sit on the birthing bed and give birth to children? God does not want that. It is against nature. That is all I can say to you."

"I know we cannot go against nature," said the black girl. "You cannot give birth to children; but women can have several husbands and still give birth to children, as long as she is not with more than one husband at the same time."

"Among God's other kinds of unfairness," said the Arab, "is one which is the ordinance He has set that the final word must be left to women to say. I cannot say it."

"What happens," said the creator, "when fifty women gather around one man, and each must say that final word?"

Japan's Withdrawal from the League of Nations Does Not Damage the League's Credibility 238

Japan Must Fulfill Treaty Obligations Within Two Years

The Vacancy of a Permanent Council Member Should Be Filled by China

丨Criticism from the German Newspaper丨

(Berlin) The German heavy industry media outlet "Deutsche Allgemeine Zeitung" commented on Japan's withdrawal from the League of Nations, stating, "Japan's military actions in Manchuria continue to expand. We believe that until now, Japan has completely disregarded various resolutions adopted by the League of Nations for peaceful resolution. Therefore, Japan's withdrawal does not harm the credibility of the League of Nations. However, even if Japan withdraws, it will not benefit the resolution of the issue, because Article 1, paragraph 3 of the League of Nations Covenant stipulates that any member of the League may withdraw from the League after giving two years' prior notice, but must fulfill all international obligations and all obligations under this Covenant at the time of withdrawal. The true meaning of this provision is difficult for politicians and jurists to agree on in their interpretation, and Japan's future attitude on this issue is also subject to varying opinions. However, regarding this matter, there is one major point that cannot be ignored, that is, the vacancy of the permanent member of the Executive Council left by Japan after its withdrawal from the League of Nations should be filled by China according to law, because among the Asian countries that are members of the League of Nations, apart from Japan, China is the most important." (12th Havas Telegram)

The Saito Cabinet Is Uneasy

The Movement to Support Hiranuma Is Gaining Momentum

The immediate problem is how the Saito Cabinet will proceed or retreat in the post-parliamentary political situation. Meanwhile, the Seiyukai, the leading party, believes that there will be a coup d'état in April or May due to the meeting between President Suzuki and Finance Minister Takahashi before parliament, and is waiting for the opportunity. Secondly, the Minseito and the House of Peers are secretly promoting the Ugaki Cabinet, but there are also those who advocate maintaining the status quo and extending the Saito Cabinet as the safest option. Therefore, there will be various plans in the post-parliamentary political situation. Will the Saito Cabinet be able to maintain the status quo, or decisively carry out a partial cabinet reshuffle, or resign and entrust the aftermath to a successor cabinet? This is a matter of great concern to all parties.

The cotton industries of Britain and Japan must never compete with each other forever. If Manchester and Osaka's cotton industries can jointly discuss this situation, he believes that a solution will be found. It is an unsound theory to regard China as a market with potential and to think that developing the Chinese market can solve the economic problems of the West. Even if one engages in the development of the Chinese market, the low standard of living of Chinese farmers will make them unable to absorb large quantities of products from other countries. At the same time, if China makes progress and becomes industrialized, it will be a competitor of Western products, rather than a consumer. Matsuoka continued by saying that he and Guo Taiqi gave a joint broadcast speech yesterday on the Far East dispute. He said that if he had known that Guo would also be speaking, he would not have wanted to speak at the same time, because after the previous session of the League of Nations General Assembly, he was no longer willing to discuss this issue with the Chinese on the same platform. Announce the Abandonment of the Republican Flag 254

The Old Imperial Flag and the Swastika Flag Are Equally Respected

▲Berlin, 12th Dispatch from Reuters German Chancellor Hitler gave a radio speech announcing that the black, red, and gold tricolor Republican flag would be abolished, and the old black, white, and red Imperial flag would still be the national flag of Germany. He also said that the Swastika flag and the Imperial flag would be equally honored, and should both be hung in all public places. Hitler called this order "a symbol of the marriage of old traditions and the revolution of the young nation," and ordered that both flags be hung in all public places across the country for three days starting on Sunday.

▲Berlin, 12th Dispatch from Havas President Hindenburg issued an order today to restore the use of the black, white, and red Imperial flag. The original text is as follows: "Today, the black, white, and red flags are flown at half-mast throughout Germany to commemorate the martyrs of the European War. The President hereby orders that from tomorrow until the national flag issue is completely resolved, the black, white, and red flag and the Swastika flag shall be hung side by side. One of these two flags is to remind people of the past glory of the German Confederation, and the other is a symbol of the victorious revival of the German nation. The combination of the two is sufficient to represent the strength of the nation and the unity of the people. Furthermore, all military agencies shall henceforth only hang the German military flag," etc.

The Strength of the Left Wing in the City Council Elections Plummets 256

In Cologne's city election, the government party still occupied a minority, winning only 44 out of 95 seats. In other towns in East Prussia, only the National Socialist Party has won an absolute majority.

▲Berlin, 12th Dispatch from Havas The situation of the re-election of the city and county councils in Prussia is still relatively calm. Only 15 people were arrested in Berlin. According to the initial news, the number of participants in the voting was less than that of the House of Representatives election last week. In the Cologne area, the number of participants in the election only reached 70% of the total number of voters. The election propaganda tools of the Social Democratic Party were all prohibited from use. Today, the party only posted announcements in front of the polling stations, urging voters to vote for the second nomination list (the second nomination list is the nomination list of the Social Democratic Party). According to the election results, the government faction, the National Socialist Party, won 86 seats, and the Nationalist faction won 27 seats, for a total of 113 seats. The opposition parties won a total of 112 seats. The number of seats won by each party is compared with the results of the 1929 election as follows:

The Current Situation in Outer Mongolia 265

The Outer Mongolian Regime is Completely Controlled by Soviet Russia

Transportation Between China and Russia Has Resumed After the Reestablishment of Diplomatic Relations

Goods from Zhangjiakou Are Being Gradually Transported to Outer Mongolia

Since the severing of diplomatic relations between China and Russia in 1926, communication with Zhangjiakou has been cut off and the Outer Mongolian regime has fallen into the hands of the Soviet Union. At that time, Chinese and Mongolian merchants still traveled back and forth, and transportation between Zhangjiakou and Kulun (Ulaanbaatar) was not completely severed. Goods from the interior could still be transported to Kulun. However, in 1929, when the Sino-Russian war broke out in Northeast China, transportation between Zhangjiakou and Kulun was completely cut off. All of the more than sixty vehicles owned by Chinese merchants operating between Zhangjiakou and Kulun were seized by the Outer Mongolian government, and the drivers were also prohibited from leaving the country. Telegraph communication between Zhangjiakou and Kulun was also cut off at this time. For several years, news between Zhangjiakou and Kulun was blocked. The more than 20,000 Chinese merchants residing in Kulun were initially able to maintain their status quo, but later, after being subjected to exorbitant taxes and levies by the Outer Mongolian government, they were almost completely exploited and are now barely surviving. Moreover, they have no way to make a living and cannot return home. They were once wealthy merchants, but now even working as small vendors is impossible. The central government is too far away to intervene in Outer Mongolia, so it sits idly by while tens of thousands of Chinese merchants are stranded and helpless, unable to be rescued. It is regrettable to see the excellent Outer Mongolian territory being controlled by the Russians. When Xu Shuzheng was appointed as the Frontier Commissioner of Outer Mongolia in 1919 and 1920, all the princes and nobles of Outer Mongolia feared the prestige of the central government. At that time, the national defense should have been actively planned and consolidated, and more troops should have been stationed in Kulun, Chakhtu, Uliastai, Tannu Uriankhai, Kobdo and other places in Outer Mongolia. Military labor could have been used for land reclamation, and the politics and education of Outer Mongolia could have been reformed. If this had been done, Outer Mongolia today would definitely not have been won over by Soviet politics. As Soviet politics has been implemented in Outer Mongolia, the youth of Outer Mongolia have been completely 麻醉 (intoxicated/influenced) by communism. All politics is controlled by the proletariat, and all power is in the hands of the Russians. The highest-ranking cadre governing Outer Mongolia is the Outer Mongolian National Defense Office. This office is a committee system, and the chairman is Russian, with nine committee members below him, both Russians and Mongolians. The internal organization is divided into a Military Committee, a Political Committee, a Labor Committee, and a Transportation Committee. All important personnel in each department are Russian. There are now 20,000 elite Mongolian soldiers who have been trained. Military officers are also Russian, stationed in key border fortresses of Outer Mongolia. All military equipment is shipped from the Soviet Union. The Outer Mongolian monarchy has long been overthrown by Soviet politics. Outer Mongolian children's and youth education textbooks are mostly translated and selected from Soviet textbooks. Russian is also taught in middle schools. Most of the middle school teachers are Russian. There are four middle schools in Outer Mongolia, two in Kulun and two in Chakhtu. As for the Outer Mongolian economy, it has long been bankrupt. Production is backward, and supply is insufficient. Local products such as furs, wool, horses, etc. have been monopolized and sold by the Russians. Now the people of Outer Mongolia are in a state of displacement, and their lives are greatly panicked. Those who are slightly more aware once launched a revolutionary wave in the spring of last year, seeking to break away from Soviet influence, but eventually disintegrated due to lack of unity. Moreover, from 1929 to 1932, transportation between Zhangjiakou and Kulun was cut off, and the domestic situation in Kulun was even more isolated. Therefore, Outer Mongolia has fallen into the hands of Soviet Russia, and the people of the country have also greatly neglected it, which is a pity. In February of this year, due to the restoration of diplomatic relations between China and Russia, Chinese and Russian merchants in Kulun planned to resume transportation between Zhangjiakou and Kulun and jointly formed the Oriental Automobile Company, sending two cars to Zhangjiakou to discuss commercial progress with the Zhangjiakou Automobile Association, intending to jointly operate the Zhangjiakou-Kulun trade with the more than 100 cars under the jurisdiction of the Zhangjiakou Automobile Association and the cars of the Kulun Oriental Automobile Company. Now the Outer Mongolian National Defense Office has approved the transit, and also allows the border Mongolian soldiers to pass through Udde (the border between Inner and Outer Mongolia) without strict inspection. Recently, the Zhangjiakou Automobile Association has also sent a car, together with the Oriental Automobile Company's car, to Kulun from Zhangjiakou on March 7 to discuss everything. The Outer Mongolian government also allows the Oriental Automobile Company to communicate with Zhangjiakou on telegrams between Zhangjiakou and Kulun. It is found that the Zhangjiakou-Kulun trade is of great significance to the development of North China's commerce, and it is also of great significance to the revitalization of Zhangjiakou's commerce. Recently, domestic goods have been able to be continuously transported to Kulun. However, the Outer Mongolian economy is controlled by the Russians, and the currency system is also unified by the Russians. Chinese currency is equivalent to waste silver after arriving in Outer Mongolia, and the Outer Mongolian taxes are extremely heavy, with a tax of 70 yuan for goods worth 100 yuan. The currency system and taxes still affect the progress of Sino-Mongolian trade, so in the future, the central government is expected to pay attention to the Outer Mongolian issue as soon as possible (March 6).

The Japanese Consul in Shantou Shields Taiwanese Smugglers 268

Customs Repeatedly Intercept Japanese Smuggling

Taiyi Maru and Hailong Maru Repeatedly Transport Sugar

Shantou Telegram. Shantou's economic severance of relations with Japan is very organized, but the other side is also doing its best to undermine it. National Salvation Associations in the urban area continue to seize enemy goods, and customs patrol ships have also repeatedly intercepted smuggled enemy ships at sea. For example, last month, the Beidou ship seized Taiyi Maru on the sea off Nanao, carrying 98 bags of white sugar. (According to the customs, foreign sugar tax is collected, and each bag must be fully paid)

The tax is 12 or 13 yuan per bag, so sugar is the main product for smugglers). It was immediately detained and returned to Shantou Port. When the Japanese consul heard the news, he immediately pleaded with the customs commissioner to return the ship, and claimed that the ship was a first offender, promised to pay the tax, and was responsible for no more smuggling in the future. However, less than a month after the Taiyi Maru incident, on the 2nd of this month, customs patrol ships again seized Hailong Maru on the sea off Shantou. Its smuggled goods were more than Taiyi Maru. According to the personnel of the customs patrol ship, on the morning of the 2nd, the Chaohai ship sailed out of Mayu Estuary to patrol. It saw a suspected electric ship near the Dezhou Lighthouse, with a Japanese flag hanging on the stern, so it sailed forward for inspection. It saw that the ship was carrying 95 tons of Javanese sugar, a total of 950 bags, and more than 20 boxes of whisky and Samsung brandy, all of which were goods subject to heavy taxes, but none of them had been taxed. There were twelve crew members on the entire ship, including one Fujianese and one Chenghai Houzhai person, and the rest were Japanese and Taiwanese. The customs officer immediately inquired about the origin and whereabouts of the ship. According to the answer, it started from Keelung, Taiwan, and went to Macau for unloading. The customs patrol ship suspected that it was smuggling, so it towed it back to Shantou Port and detained it in front of the customs. The customs commissioner specially ordered the shipowner to go to the customs for questioning. According to the shipowner, the goods on the ship were returning to Taiwan from Hong Kong. Because of the waves the night before, it approached the mountainside to hide. The customs commissioner said that his statements were inconsistent, one because Macau also needs sugar, and there is no need to transport it from Taiwan. Second, because Taiwan is a famous sugar-producing area, there is no need to transport it from Hong Kong. As for encountering wind and hiding in Dezhou on the way, it is even more absurd. However, it is heard that the Japanese consul will come forward to shield the smuggled ship again. (March 3)

Statistical Table of Salt Tax Revenue in the Past Twenty Years 269

Tax Revenue Decreased During the Northern Expedition

Gradual Increase After 1920

Central tax revenue is mainly composed of customs and salt taxes. In terms of salt tax, the national statistics, from 1914 to last year, the annual income in the past 20 years is as follows: 1914 (1914) was 50,908,402.77 (unit: yuan, that is, the above is more than 50.09 million), 1915 was 55,972,7870.17, 1916 was 63,016,467.37, 1917 was 63,988,787.20, 1918 was 68,890,500.92, 1919 was 71,980,277.26, 1920 was 77,046,032.96, 1921 was 82,370,694.90, 1922 was 87,762,828.55, 1923 was 79,883,180.44, 1924 was 75,888,324.69, 1925 was 79,144,093.06, 1926 was 77,927,522.29, 1927 was 55,268,508.42, 1928 was 58,541,852.44, 1929 was 69,723,002.39, 1930 was 139,391,487.19, 1931 was 176,651,151.52, and 1932 (last year) was 160,833,648.12. According to the above, there was no increase or decrease from 1916 to 1926. In 1927 and 1928, the tax revenue was greatly reduced due to the military affairs of the Northern Expedition. It was not until the national unification in 1930 that people celebrated peace, and the salt tax also increased rapidly.

Further Negotiations on Huangpu Steamer Dispute 282

The Huangpu steamer of the British-owned Swire Shipping Company, operating the Shanghai-Hankou route, issued a company notice on February 15th to lay off twenty-three of the coolies from the steamer's steerage. The coolies, believing the company intended to oppress them, collectively protested, submitting several petitions to party and government authorities requesting intervention. The steerage coolies' association also ordered all eighty-six coolies not to leave the ship without permission and to continue working as usual. After several mediations by party and government authorities, the company agreed to increase the number of coolies to thirty, adding seven more. After the coolies were advised, they also relented somewhat, agreeing to fifty. The steamer arrived in Shanghai the day before yesterday (the 11th), and representatives from the party and government went to negotiate, but no agreement was reached due to the significant difference in the proposed number of coolies. Today, the company again invited party and government authorities. ▲Escorted to Court This Morning for Trial

They were taken to the police station. Investigation revealed that Wang and Shen, on the fourth of last month at 9:30 AM, had led a gang armed with weapons to break into the accounting house rented by Wu Minsheng at 196 Tianjin Road, robbing them of $4,685 in cash and silver dollars. They were detained and escorted to the Eighth Criminal Division of the First Special District Court this morning. The police lawyer, Wang Yaotang, stated the case, saying that Wang and Shen had confessed to the robbery at the police station, having conspired with accomplices still at large in room 10 of the Yongle Inn on Fujian Road on February 3, and continuing the discussion at 6 AM the next day in room 427 of the Zhongnan Inn on Edward Road, deciding to commit the robbery. They set out at 9:30 AM with five people. Shen stood guard downstairs, while the others went upstairs. After obtaining the loot, they convened to divide the spoils. Wang received $250, and Shen received $50. Yesterday, the detectives learned that Wang and others were staying at the Donghua Inn and went to arrest them. Chen Erchu was arrested as well because he was staying with Wang and Shen. The police charged Wang and Shen with armed robbery under the criminal law. Chen Erchu's detention was requested. Subsequently, Wu Minsheng filed a case, detailing the robbery, and stating that the defendant Wang Lao Si had previously worked for him. Judge Qian Wenji briefly questioned the defendants and ordered them detained for further questioning in seven days.

Sino-Russian Communication Realized 284

Charges Based on Ural Mountains as Boundary Between Asia and Europe

A reporter from the Huadong News Agency inquired with the person in charge of the telegraph office this afternoon about Sino-Russian communication. They were informed that Sino-Russian wireless communication had been officially implemented starting yesterday. These telegrams are sent via the Zhenru International Radio Station. The charging method is based on distance. Areas west of the Ural Mountains in Russia are considered part of Europe, with a charge of $1.95 per word. Areas east of the Ural Mountains are considered part of Asia, with a charge of $1.45 per word.

Lin Pengju and Sister Trafficking Children 286

Children Bought from Chongming and Qidong

Fujian native Lin Pengju and his sister Lin Yuying recently bought two children in Chongming County. At around 8 AM the day before yesterday, they boarded the Zhoushan Maru at the Yangshupu Wharf, intending to return to their hometown to sell them for profit. Detectives Wang Guangqi, Hu Guangrong, and Yang Zhaoqing of the Hongkou Police Station learned of this and, along with Detective Chief Shi Enjian, secretly boarded the ship and arrested the Lin siblings. The two children, one five years old and one two years old, were also taken to the police station and detained separately. This morning, lawyer Zhang Tianyin of the police station stated that the police charged the defendants with human trafficking under Article 257, Section 2 of the Criminal Code. Investigation revealed that the defendants conspired with Xu Ziying, who is still at large, to go to Chongming and Qidong counties, where they bought the five-year-old boy for $100 and the two-year-old child for $52 from impoverished families. Because both defendants are from Fujian and do not speak the local dialect, Xu Ziying handled everything. Their plan was to bring the children back to their hometown, sell them to wealthy families, and share the profits with Xu, who would then purchase more children. Xu lives in a shanty in Yangshupu, Taopeng Road. The detectives rushed to arrest him, but he had already fled. It is unclear whether the children were abducted in Chongming and Qidong or in Shanghai. They requested a postponement for further investigation. Questioned, defendant Lin Pengju stated that because he and his sister Yuying had no sons, they entrusted Xu, who is still at large, to purchase them as adopted sons. The parents of both children signed contracts at the time of purchase, one in the First Gang of Qidong County and one in Renhe Township of the same county, but the purchase documents were lost in haste. His remaining testimony was evasive. His sister Lin Yuying testified that she did not know Xu and had not gone to Chongming. She asked her brother Lin Pengju to buy the two-year-old child as her son. Judge Wu Zehan ordered them to be detained separately for further verification. Lawyer Zhang of the police station requested that the two children be temporarily sent to the Women and Children's Relief Society for care. The court approved this.

Young Man Commits Suicide Due to Extreme Poverty 287

This morning at 6:30 AM, a young man was found hanged at the entrance of Chongde Lane on Bansongyuan Road in the city. The officer at post number 41 discovered him, but it was too late to save him. The local bailiff reported it to the local court for an autopsy. The deceased was wearing a blue cloth short shirt and trousers and running shoes, appeared to be in his twenties, and resembled a discharged soldier. He committed suicide due to extreme poverty.

Robbery on Xuexi Street Last Night 288

The home of Fan Songliu at number 2, Qinli Lane, Xuexi Street in the Nanshi district was robbed last night at around 9 PM, just after dinner. Four robbers wearing gabardine short shirts and trousers suddenly arrived. They all spoke with a northern Jiangsu accent. Two robbers rushed into the living room, each taking out a pistol, and forbade anyone from making a sound. The other two robbers quickly went out to stand guard, preventing any unexpected events. As a result, one hundred silver dollars, fifty dollars in paper money, two gold rings, and one silver bracelet were robbed. After the robbery, they quickly fled into the alleys to the north and south. By the time nearby officers arrived, the four robbers had vanished without a trace.

First Phase of Seven-Province Highway Construction Nears Completion 289

National Economic Council Proceeding with Second Phase

The National Economic Council is proceeding with the second phase of the Seven-Province Highway construction. A reporter from the Datong News Agency interviewed the person in charge of the council this morning, inquiring about the current status. They received a detailed response, recorded below.

(Planned Content) According to the Seven-Province Highway plan drafted by the National Economic Council's specially appointed League of Nations road construction experts, Mr. Pootly and Mr. Okaski, the entire project is divided into two phases. The first phase is to complete the Beijing-Shanghai, Beijing-Changsha, Beijing-Wuhu, and Suzhou-Jiaxing highways, totaling approximately 1,600 kilometers in length. Currently, the Beijing-Shanghai Highway is nearing completion, and the Suzhou-Wujiang section of the Suzhou-Jiaxing Highway has also been completed. The Beijing-Changsha and Beijing-Wuhu highways are scheduled to be completed by the end of May. Then, in early June, the second phase of the project, which is larger in scope than the first phase, will begin. The total length of the highway is over 6,700 kilometers. According to the National Economic Council, the complete highway is critical for military transportation during this time of national crisis. Therefore, it is proposed to order the construction departments of all provinces to complete the construction of the highways within their jurisdiction this year. At the same time, it is also proposed to consult with the Ministry of Military Affairs to order the troops stationed in each province to cooperate in the work. The government will provide funding to facilitate the progress of the project.

(Decision Steps) Regarding the steps for proceeding with the second phase of the project and the budget for funding, the National Economic Council convened engineers from the construction departments of each province in Beijing from the 6th to the 9th of this month to discuss solutions. The result was a decision that engineers from the construction departments of each province should first construct bridges and culverts along the highways in their respective provinces, and then proceed with the road surface. The Economic Council will send personnel to each province to supervise the progress, with the goal of completing the project as soon as possible. After the national government directly allocates funds to the council, the council will then distribute them to each province.

(Full Line Opening) As for the date of the full line opening of the Beijing-Shanghai, Beijing-Wuhu, Beijing-Changsha, and Suzhou-Jiaxing highways completed in the first phase, based on the current situation, it should be realized in mid-month. League of Nations road experts Mr. Pootly and Mr. Okaski test-drove the Beijing-Shanghai Highway on the 3rd of this month and found it very satisfactory.

Commentary

Military Pledge 290

— Geng

This is an ironclad fact: when the brutal Japanese occupied our Northeast, it was without firing a shot. It wasn't that their soldiers were "descended from the heavens," but that our "policy of non-resistance" helped them succeed. Having tasted such an enormous and easy advantage, the brutal Japanese not only remained unsatisfied, but also sought more, casting greedy eyes everywhere, coveting our Jehol province and seizing it as easily as reaching into a bag. The reason for this was that Jehol abandoned its duty, retreating without a fight. In this situation, it is clear that one side has retreated to a point where it is being criticized both internally and externally, and where it can no longer tolerate it; while the other side is still elated, taking one step further after another. As the saying goes, "Even a trapped beast will fight to the death," so it is no wonder that our young marshal was provoked into a thunderous rage, and "in anger over the loss of Jehol, volunteered to assemble all the basic units of the Northeast Army to take on the front-line combat, taking responsibility as the vanguard, making a 'military pledge' to recapture Chengde within a set number of days." (See the 10th Shishi News and 9th this newspaper Evening News) Good heavens! "The good do not come, and those who come are not good." The Japanese better quickly prepare ships to cross to the east, for the result will certainly be that they "cannot swallow it!"

As for what a "military pledge" is, in this year of unclear rewards and punishments, perhaps some have forgotten its seriousness? For example, Guan Yu, who released Cao Cao on Huarong Road, was ordered by Kongming to be "dragged out and beheaded," all because of the "military pledge"! The "military pledge" that the young marshal is willing to make this time is undoubtedly "no small matter," although its full depth remains unfathomable. Judging from its meaning, it is, of course, to swear to recover Chengde within the specified time (naturally not a long time); if Chengde is not recovered, he swears not to return alive, which is the same as what was previously said, "to defend the national border with blood and life." If the stars of the general are high, and the solar stars resolve the situation, and enemy bullets dare not approach, and he is forced to return alive, then because "there is no joking in the military," he should also show the true colors of a hero, and frankly accept the serious punishment of being "dragged out and beheaded," no, dragged out and shot. This majestic "military pledge," which is enough to make the enemy tremble in fear, if indeed made by the young marshal and carried out by the young marshal himself, would heaven and earth not be shaken by it, and would soldiers not drink blood for it? Just as Fan Li did not commit suicide to wash away the shame of Kuaiji, and Cao Mo did not die to erase the humiliation of three defeats, but in the end avenged Goujian and repaid the shame of the State of Lu, it is clear that our young marshal will also make this earth-shattering "military pledge" to recover Chengde, in order to wash away the great shame and humiliation of the fall of Shenyang, the retreat from Jinzhou, and the loss of Yuguan! Therefore, towards this "military pledge" that gives us great hope, how can we not stand in solemn respect and pay our sincere tribute!

Unfortunately, Mr. Chiang knows that he is bragging and does not believe him. He still asks him to use one of his thirty-six stratagems, fearing that he will not only fail to recover Chengde, but also send away Tianjin and Beiping. He can only accept his deep kindness, respectfully thanking him but not accepting his offer.

A Hard Battle 291

— Bing

Dongyang previously did not believe it, thinking that even if it happened, it would be accidental. Even though the bragging in the newspapers every day was so intense, with Ah Fu raping Gendi and Ah Da seducing Xiao Mao, when you look at "Ah Fu liked women, and Gendi was young and promiscuous, resulting in seduction, so they were lovey-dovey, flying together as a couple," you can know the truth of the matter, but if the matter breaks down, the responsibility lies entirely with Ah Fu. Ah Fu rapes Gendi, but in fact, when they commit adultery, Gendi is also fully in agreement.

So, although the newspapers are full of such records, Dongyang still does not have confidence, believing that women always escape a portion of the responsibility.

So, what he says to his wife is naturally very doubtful, saying that it is all about whether a woman is proper or improper. This might be because he is in front of his wife, so his tone is particularly heavy, but his wife only says that he is an outsider, no wonder he doesn't understand, and that one day he will have to see it for himself.

This is the third time. His wife dragged her tired body, her unsettled soul, and walked back in a panic. At first, she was speechless, then she cried for a while. Finally, she said to her husband:

"I really don't want to do this unlucky work anymore. Those bastards dare to make passes at me in front of me. Damn it..." She cried again.

"What happened? Tell me properly!" Dongyang asked comfortingly.

"You know, that stinking slut, Fourth Sister De, is always flirting, and that feminine air attracts those scoundrels, making them drool. As a result, in the alley..." the matter breaks out, and they become angry from embarrassment. No wonder everyone looks down on her, and no wonder you once said that women have to take responsibility."

"As for that slut, Sixth Sister Xiao, I've seen her several times with my own eyes. A good-for-nothing named Peng flirted with her, and she just went along with it. As for me, I never bat an eye at anyone, let alone pay attention to those things. Today, that pig Luo, who's surnamed Wang, kept standing next to my spinning machine, smiling and making all sorts of strange faces. I didn't care and told him straight:

"Am I not doing a good job? Write a note and give it to the accountant to fire me!"

Instead, he pouted and smiled sweetly, saying:

"I never thought you would be so fierce! Are you tired? I'll wait for you at the XX Road intersection at 8:30 tonight. How about we go see a movie together!"

"I was really furious, so I turned around and left. I'm not doing this damn work anymore!"

Hearing this, Dongyang suddenly perked up.

"Ha, those bastards are really like that? Ha, wait for me to go!" He immediately stood up, flexing his sleeves.

"That would be best. Let's go together. That bastard is definitely waiting for me at the XX Road intersection, thinking that I'll really fall for his trap. Go, let's go together!"

His wife pointed out the man standing by the tram platform, wearing a Western suit, holding a newspaper, and Dongyang rushed forward, throwing him to the ground with force, followed by punches and kicks. Suddenly, Dongyang felt two punches in his back, and his back was throbbing with pain. Undoubtedly, it was some bodyguard of the Wang good-for-nothing who had come.

In the midst of the difficult fight, three or four police officers came and, without saying a word, dragged Dongyang and his wife into jail, while that Wang good-for-nothing walked away leisurely, as if singing a triumphal song. The police officers just looked on.

"If you don't do this unlucky work, you have to sit in this unlucky jail, and it's even dragged you down," his wife said.

"Yes, this is the reality of today's society! But at least Wang good-for-nothing suffered a good lesson from us! What's needed now is how to teach those dog policemen a lesson," her husband, Dongyang, said.

Escape 292

— Xianxia

At noon, in front of the M school gate, it was like an exhibition, with everything: selling squid, braised spiced beans, egg slices, dried tofu, water chestnuts, lottery food, and even stationery and rubber bands.

The innocent and lively children, before class started, were always surrounding these food vendors, some buying food to chew on with relish, others enthusiastically playing the lottery. Those without money could only watch others with envious eyes. The children were not stingy in taking money out of their pockets, which was also the only guarantee of livelihood for the vendors.

"Here they come! The big guys are coming!" A vendor selling spiced beans near the road shouted as he quickly ran away. At this time, the lively atmosphere suddenly became tense.

A police officer, as fat as a pig and wearing a uniform, chased after them. The vendors desperately ran for their lives. The squid vendor hid under a pile of wood across the street, the spiced bean vendor squatted next to a trash can, and others fled elsewhere. In an instant, they all disappeared. But as soon as the police officer walked past, the scene in front of the school gate returned to its original state.

"Ah yo! Sir, please forgive me!" The police officer came back from the other side, and the vendors ran away for the second time. An old woman in her fifties who sold water chestnuts was caught by the police officer because she was too slow to run. She begged him in every way, but she could not move the police officer's heart. Then, he kicked the basket of peeled and white water chestnuts onto the ground. She had no choice but to squat on the ground, gather them up, and walk away with tears in her eyes.

A child selling rubber bands, about ten years old, holding a bunch of rubber bands in his hand, was also seen by the police officer because he was not agile enough to hide. First, he received two slaps, followed by a scolding.

For the sake of making a living, the vendors had to endure such suffering.

Saturday Afternoon 293

— Qiling

Saturday afternoons have always been a time for students to rest or play, with no classes.

Because the curriculum in middle schools is relatively light, the Ministry of Education this year issued an order that all middle schools should have classes on Saturday afternoons, adding more courses. As a result, the students inevitably expressed some boredom (?).

"How annoying! Today afternoon was supposed to be for playing ball, but we have to go to class."

"I can't see the 3:00 movie anymore."

"I had a date with my girlfriend today, but I'm tied up with schoolwork, so I have to reschedule."

"………………………………"

Various different complaints were made by every student, all cursing Saturday afternoon classes. They never thought about who would benefit from Saturday afternoon classes!

As fate would have it, the course on this particular Saturday afternoon was geography, which everyone considered unimportant. Since the homework was not important and the teacher was easy to talk to, some people were absent without reason, and others reported their attendance and then escaped from the classroom pretending to go to the toilet. They thought they had won, and they went to do what they wanted to do. Out of sixty-odd people in the grade, only half remained, going through the motions.

"Teacher! Please take attendance again." The headmaster came to inspect the classroom, and because he saw that there were too few people, he became suspicious and took the roll book to take attendance again.

As a result, excluding those who were absent without reason, there were eight people who escaped during class.

The next morning, a long rectangular piece of paper was posted on the headmaster's bulletin board, writing:

"××, ××, ... eight people are skipping class; each will be given a major demerit as a warning to others. Headmaster Bai."

…………………………

Alas! You reap what you sow.

Shop Assistant Correspondence

Jealousy or Laziness? 294

— Shen Liewen

Dear Editor,

Your Shop Assistant Correspondence column is for us shop assistants, workers, and apprentices to resolve our doubts and difficulties. Since its inception, we have received many benefits. Now I have another difficulty, and I would still like you to give me guidance. The matter is like this: before "January 28th," I worked at a × paint factory in Zhabei. After the war, of course, I was unemployed. Although I can't talk about academic qualifications in the paint industry, I can say that I'm not bad at it, based on my ten years of experience. About half a year after being unemployed, after many twists and turns, I found work in a certain paint factory in western Shanghai: not only can I solve my livelihood problem, but I also have the opportunity to make use of my previous experience. I was overjoyed. Now the products in the factory are much worse than the products in the factory where I used to work, but the raw materials are the same, just the methods are different. Because I am "eating the well water of the family and helping the family," I became enthusiastic and advised the technician to change to my method, so that the products would become increasingly excellent and the sales would increase. But he always ignored me and refused to adopt it. I really don't know if he is "enduring" or lazy! In short, my experience, if it goes on like this, will never be brought into play! Sir, what do you think I should do? (Omitted) Shen Liewen respectfully

×　　×　　×　　×

Editor's note: Chinese people have a kind of inferiority, which is "not only unwilling to improve themselves, but also unwilling to allow others to improve." His motives are nothing more than two, which Han Yu called "laziness and jealousy." If this kind of inferiority is not eradicated one day, China will really have no hope one day. The technician in Shen Jun's factory is deeply poisoned by this. We believe that if Shen Jun really has real experience and the certainty of improvement, you should discuss it with the manager, and he will definitely take it. Because improving products is directly beneficial to him. As for the technician, he is afraid that once you succeed, he will have to step down. So if you want him to adopt your method, it is really like seeking the skin of a tiger, and there is absolutely no hope.

Fiction

Fleeting Moments in a Dream (Continued) 295

— Qin Shouou

(II) The Beginning in a Dream

Forty-three years before the events of the previous section, Dr. Wu Yi was born in a small, remote county along the Beijing-Shanghai Railway line: that was K County, famous throughout the land for the inexplicably named "Old Master" three characters.

At that time, there was no Beijing-Shanghai Railway, nor any small steamships. The transportation between K County and the outside world was unimaginably inconvenient; and the people who lived in K County mostly adhered to the ancient saying, "While parents are alive, do not travel far." They were reluctant to move their bodies more than ten miles away from their homes. However, during a certain period—that is, during the period when a large number of "Scholars and Recommended Men" were produced—twice a year, as usual, there would always be a group of bookish friends who had spent ten, twenty, thirty, or forty years in their studies like widowers, embracing gorgeous dreams as bright as brocade, bidding farewell to their parents and wives, and hurriedly setting off in groups on the only means of transportation in the interior of 18th-century China—sailing boats—heading towards the location of those pigeon-box-like examination halls. Of course, when they returned, occasionally a few would hire large official boats, raise yellow flags, and return—those were a few exceptions, carp leaping over the dragon gate. Most, however, still returned in small sailing boats.

That autumn, as usual, another group of fame-and-fortune-seeking young people, middle-aged people, and old people were preparing to leave their hometowns and do a "flower gambling" style illusory dream. The barefooted men who steered the sailing boats were also busy running on the streets; old customers were naturally unwilling to be sacrificed, and new customers were eager to be won over.

"Second Master! Needless to say, you must give us some lucky money!" The Wu residence on South Street was a well-known family in K County, full of scholarly descendants: Second Master Wu was one of the best among them. Although he had returned without success three times, he was still young and had great hope: so this time, in the heart of Old Mao, the boatman, he was sure to have another good customer.

"I'm not going this time!" Second Master Wu gave him an unexpectedly disappointing reply in a very gloomy manner.

"Don't talk nonsense! Second Brother! Don't miss your future!" Before Old Mao could try to win over Second Master Wu again, First Master Wu, in his position as the elder brother, sternly refuted his words.

"That's right! Second Master is guaranteed to pass this time, he should definitely go!" Old Mao, having received the help of First Master Wu, encouraged him with extra force.

"But, I..." Second Master Wu still wanted to struggle, and this was to his elder brother.

"The eldest brother is like a father, can you disobey my words?" First Master Wu got angry and decided to enforce it. "Old Mao, reserve that middle cabin for us brothers!"

Of course, the younger brother could not defy the words of the elder brother; this was the rule of a family of scholars and etiquette. Second Master Wu submitted to this rule: but at the time, his attitude was extraordinarily flustered and melancholic. For a long while, he paced back and forth in his study, then took the opportunity to slip out and went straight to the residence of a family named Cheng across the street.

The Cheng family used to be a wealthy family, and they are still not poor, but all the men in their family died early, leaving only a widow in her forties and a Miss in her teens. Second Master Wu, not knowing by what chance, had fallen in love with this Miss, so much so that the Miss's belly had swelled as high as a young mistress's; but, unfortunately, Second Master Wu already had a lawfully wedded young mistress at home, and First Master Wu absolutely forbade his younger brother from marrying a second wife, so a very serious problem arose.

But Miss Cheng's belly was getting higher day by day, and the crystallization of love was about to be born; so the widowed Mrs. Cheng, in the unofficial capacity of prospective mother-in-law, ordered Second Master Cheng not to go to the examination. However, on the other hand, his elder brother insisted on forcing him to make a struggle for family honor; Second Master Cheng was in a dilemma, truly in a very awkward situation!

"After returning from this examination, no matter what, I will definitely find a way to marry you and bring you home! I would rather separate from my elder brother than let you down!" After some internal debate, Second Master Wu's desire for advancement prevailed over his affection for his children, and he decided to go to the examination. He asked his lover, Miss Cheng, for her consent with an extremely sincere attitude.

Of course, Miss Cheng couldn't just agree to him; later, he had to make a few extremely venomous oaths—the only way to persuade women—and Miss Cheng herself had a new realization, knowing that even if Second Master Wu didn't leave, it wouldn't relieve her pain during childbirth, so she agreed.

On the seventh day after Second Master Wu left K County, a promising child emerged from Miss Cheng's belly. The Cheng widow's house was filled with a very mysterious joy.

…………………………………………

One month, two months passed... First Master Wu returned from the examination, bringing back a coffin, announcing the bad news that Second Master Wu had contracted an illness and died in the examination hall.
